# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes APF QueueSet Deep-Dive

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an algorithmic deep-dive on APF QueueSet behavior, dispatch flow, and fairness tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the APF QueueSet subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

---

**Document structure:**

1. **Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies** — Explains that the APF QueueSet implements WFQ-based fair queuing for API server request admission. Maps upstream (HTTP filter → classification → hashing → `StartRequest`) and downstream (the actual request handler) boundaries, and enumerates all peer dependencies in a table.

2. **Key Components and Responsibility Split** — Covers nine components:
   - `configController`: FlowSchema/PLC config digestion, request classification, borrowing
   - `QueueSetFactory`/`QueueSetCompleter`: two-phase construction design and why it exists
   - `queueSet`: the core engine with its global virtual-time meter `currentR`
   - `queue`: per-flow virtual queue with `nextDispatchR` as the WFQ state
   - `request`: per-request tracking with the `promise.WriteOnce` dispatch signal
   - `fifo`/`requestFIFO`: O(1) incremental aggregate sum for shuffle-sharding
   - `promise.WriteOnce`: lock-free cross-goroutine dispatch signaling
   - Work estimators (list, mutating, two-phase seat model)
   - Shuffle-sharding `Dealer` algorithm

3. **End-to-End Flow** — Seven concrete steps with code references: classification → shuffle sharding → reject/enqueue → dispatch via virtual finish time → waiting via `promise.Get` → execution/completion → `nextDispatchR` adjustment with actual vs. estimated service time feedback.

4. **Borrowing Algorithm** — How `updateBorrowing` periodically redistributes unused concurrency across priority levels using the `computeConcurrencyAllocation` bounded-proportional-allocation algorithm (`conc_alloc.go`).

5. **Failure Modes, Limits, and Tradeoffs** — Rejection paths, context cancel
... (truncated)

73-assistanttext-
The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. The background exploration agent has also completed, confirming the analysis is comprehensive and accurate.

The document covers the full APF QueueSet subsystem across 8 major sections:

1. **Purpose and boundaries** — where the subsystem sits in the API server's request path, what it touches upstream (HTTP filter → classification) and downstream (the actual handler callback), and all peer dependencies.

2. **Component responsibilities** — nine components dissected: `configController`, the two-phase factory, `queueSet`, `queue`, `request`, `fifo`, `promise.WriteOnce`, the work estimators, and the shuffle-sharding `Dealer`.

3. **End-to-end flow** — seven concrete steps from HTTP arrival through classification, shuffle sharding, enqueue/reject, virtual-time-based dispatch, cross-goroutine waiting via `promise.Get`, handler execution, and `nextDispatchR` adjustment with actual-vs-estimated service time feedback.

4. **Borrowing algorithm** — how `updateBorrowing` (every 10 seconds) uses time-weighted seat-demand statistics from the `Integrator` and `computeConcurrencyAllocation` (bounded proportional allocation) to dynamically redistribute concurrency between priority levels.

5. **Failure modes and tradeoffs** — reject-path conditions (AND of queue-full + concurrency-full), context timeout/cancellation handling, oversized-request starvation behavior, the fixed 3ms service estimate limitation, and round-robin tie-breaking semantics.

6. **Extension and customization hooks** — six injection points with associated risks: `promiseFactoryFactory`, `eventclock`, `WorkEstimatorFunc`, the `QueueSetFactory` interface, `MaxSeatsTracker`, and operator-facing API object configuration.

The fields listed before the lock\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\n73: //\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\n75: // suffix \"Locked\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\n76: // whose name does not end in \"Locked\" either acquires the lock or\n77: // does not care about locking.\n78: //\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\n80: // \"ToBoundLocked\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`.                c,\n178: \t\tpromiseFactoryFactory: promiseFactoryFactory,\n179: \t}\n180: }\n181: \n182: func (qsf *queueSetFactory) BeginConstruction(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig, reqsGaugePair {\n185: \t\treturn nil, err\n186: \t}\n187: \treturn &queueSetCompleter{\n188: \t\tfactory:              qsf,\n189: \t\treqsGaugePair:        reqsGaugePair,\n190: \t\texecSeatsGauge: non-nil Dealer if the config is valid and\n197: // calls for one, and returns a non-nil error if the given config is\n198: // invalid.\n199: func checkConfig(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig) (*shufflesharding.Dealer, error) {\n200: \tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues <= 0 {\n201: \t\treturn nil, nil\n202: \t}\n203: \tdealer, err := shufflesharding.NewDealer(qCfg.DesiredNumQueues, dealer, err\n208: }\n209: \n210: func (qsc *queueSetCompleter) Complete(dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig) fq.QueueSet {\n211: \tqs := qsc.theSet\n212: \tif qs == nil {\n213: \t\tqs = &queueSet{\n214: \t\t\tclock:                    qsc.factory.clock,\n215: \t\t\testimatedServiceDuration: 3 * time.Millisecond,\n216: \t\t\treqsGaugePair:            qsc.reqsGaugePair,\n217: \t\t\texecSeatsGauge:           qsc.execSeatsGauge,\n218: \t\t\tseatDemandIntegrator:     qsc.seatDemandIntegrator,\n219: \t\t\tqCfg:                     qsc.qCfg,\n220: \t\t\tcurrentR:                 0,\n221: qsc.factory.promiseFactoryFactory(qs)\n225: \t}\n226: \tqs.setConfiguration(context.Background(), qsc.qCfg, qsc.dealer, dCfg)\n227: \treturn qs\n228: }\n229: \n230: // createQueues is a helper method for initializing an array of n queues\n231: func createQueues(n, baseIndex int) []*queue {\n232: \tfqqueues := make([]*queue, n)\n233: \tfor i := 0; i < n; i++ {\n234: \t\tfqqueues[i] = &queue{index: fq.QueuingConfig) (fq.QueueSetCompleter, error) {\n240: \tdealer, err := checkConfig(qCfg)\n241: \tif err != nil {\n242: \t\treturn nil, err\n243: \t}\n244: \treturn &queueSetCompleter{\n245: \t\ttheSet: qs,\n246: \t\tqCfg:   qCfg,\n247: \t\tdealer: dealer}, nil\n248: }\n249: \n250: // setConfiguration is used to set the configuration for a queueSet.\n251: // Update handling for when fields are updated is handled here as well -\n252: // eg: if DesiredNum is increased, setConfiguration reconciles by\n253: // adding more queues.\n254: func (qs *queueSet) setConfiguration(ctx context.Context, qCfg fq.QueuingConfig, dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer, dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig) {\n255: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)\n256: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n257: \n258: \tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > 0 {\n259: \t\t// Adding queues is the only thing that requires immediate action\n260: \t\t// Removing queues is handled by attrition, removing a queue when\n261: \t\t// it goes qs.qCfg.HandSize\n270: \t}\n271: \n272: \tqs.qCfg = qCfg\n273: \tqs.dCfg = dCfg\n274: \tqs.dealer = dealer\n275: \tqll := qCfg.QueueLengthLimit\n276: \tif qll < 1 {\n277: \t\tqll = 1\n278: \t}\n279: \tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > 0 {\n280: \t\tqll *= qCfg.DesiredNumQueues\n281: \t}\n282: \tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.SetDenominator(float64(qll))\n283: \tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsExecuting.SetDenominator(float64(dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator))\n284: \tqs.execSeatsGauge.SetDenominator(float64(dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator))\n285: \n286: \tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n287: }\n288: \n289: // A decision about a request\n290: type requestDecision int\n291: \n292: // Values passed through a request's decision\n293: const (\n294: \t// Serve this one\n295: \tdecisionExecute requestDecision = iota\n296: \n297: \t// This one's context timed out / was canceled\n298: \tdecisionCancel\n299: )\n300: \n301: // StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  We take the\n302: // approach of updating the metrics about total requests queued and\n303: // executing at each point where there is a change in that quantity,\n304: // because the metrics --- and only the metrics --- track that\n305: // quantity per FlowSchema.\n306: // The queueSet's promiseFactory is invoked once if the returned Request is non-nil,\n307: // not invoked if the Request is nil.\n308: func (qs *queueSet) StartRequest(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) (fq.Request, bool) {\n309: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)\n310: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n311: \tvar req *request\n312: \n313: \t// ========================================================================\n314: \t// Step 0:\n315: \t// Apply only concurrency limit, if zero queues desired\n316: \tif qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 1 {\n317: \t\tif !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats()) {\n318: \t\t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v because %d seats are asked for, %d seats are in use (%d are executing) and the limit is %d\",\n319: \t\t\t\tqs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2, workEstimate, qs.totSeatsInUse, qs.totRequestsExecuting, qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)\n320: \t\t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n321: \t\t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"concurrency-limit\")\n322: \t\t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n323: \t\t}\n324: \t\treq = qs.dispatchSansQueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n325: \t\treturn req, false\n326: \t}\n327: \n328: \t// ========================================================================\n329: \t// Step 1:\n330: \t// 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n331: \t// 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n332: \t// we are at max queue length\n333: \t// 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n334: \treq = qs.shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2, queueNoteFn)\n335: \t// req == nil means that the request was rejected - no remaining\n336: \t// concurrency shares and at max queue length already\n337: \tif req == nil {\n338: \t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v due to queue full\", qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n339: \t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n340: \t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"queue-full\")\n341: \t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n342: \t}\n343: \n344: \t// ========================================================================\n345: \t// Step 2:\n346: \t// The next step is to invoke the method that dequeues as much\n347: \t// as possible.\n348: \t// This method runs a loop, as long as there are non-empty\n349: \t// queues and the number currently executing is less than the\n350: \t// assured concurrency value.  The body of the loop uses the\n351: \t// fair queuing technique to pick a queue and dispatch a\n352: \t// request from that queue.\n353: \tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n354: \n355: \treturn req, false\n356: }\n357: \n358: // ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory is the promiseFactoryFactory that\n359: // a queueSetFactory would ordinarily use.\n360: // Test code might use something different.\n361: func ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory(qs *queueSet) promiseFactory {\n362: \treturn promise.NewWriteOnce\n363: }\n364: \n365: // MaxSeats returns the maximum number of seats this request requires, it is\n366: // the maxumum of the two - WorkEstimate.InitialSeats, WorkEstimate.FinalSeats.\n367: func (req *request) MaxSeats() int {\n368: \treturn req.workEstimate.MaxSeats()\n369: }\n370: \n371: func (req *request) InitialSeats() int {\n372: \treturn int(req.workEstimate.InitialSeats)\n373: }\n374: \n375: func (req *request) NoteQueued(inQueue bool) {\n376: \tif req.queueNoteFn != nil {\n377: \t\treq.queueNoteFn(inQueue)\n378: \t}\n379: }\n380: \n381: func (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n382: \texec, idle := req.wait()\n383: \tif !exec {\n384: \t\treturn idle\n385: \t}\n386: \tfunc() {\n387: \t\tdefer func() {\n388: \t\t\tidle = req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n389: \t\t}()\n390: \n391: \t\texecFn()\n392: \t}()\n393: \n394: \treturn idle\n395: }\n396: \n397: func (req *request) wait() (bool, bool) {\n398: \tqs := req.qs\n399: \n400: \t// ========================================================================\n401: \t// Step 3:\n402: \t// The final step is to wait on a decision from\n403: \t// somewhere and then act on it.\n404: \tdecisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n405: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n406: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n407: \tif req.waitStarted {\n408: \t\t// This can not happen, because the client is forbidden to\n409: \t\t// call Wait twice on the same request\n410: \t\tklog.Errorf(\"Duplicate call to the Wait method!  Immediately returning execute=false.  QueueSet=%s, startTime=%s, descr1=%#+v, descr2=%#+v\", req.qs.qCfg.Name, req.startTime, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n411: \t\treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n412: \t}\n413: \treq.waitStarted = true\n414: \tswitch decisionAny {\n415: \tcase decisionCancel: // handle in code following this switch\n416: \tcase decisionExecute:\n417: \t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Dispatching request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n418: \t\treturn true, false\n419: \tdefault:\n420: \t\t// This can not happen, all possible values are handled above\n421: \t\tklog.Errorf(\"QS(%s): Impossible decision (type %T, value %#+v) for request %#+v %#+v!  Treating as cancel\", qs.qCfg.Name, decisionAny, decisionAny, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n422: \t}\n423: \t// TODO(aaron-prindle) add metrics for this case\n424: \tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Ejecting request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n425: \t// remove the request from the queue as its queue wait time has exceeded\n426: \tqueue := req.queue\n427: \tif req.removeFromQueueLocked() != nil {\n428: \t\tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n429: \t\tqs.totRequestsWaiting--\n430: \t\tqs.totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n431: \t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n432: \t\tqs.totRequestsCancelled++\n433: \t\tmetrics.AddReject(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, \"time-out\")\n434: \t\tmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -1)\n435: \t\tmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -req.MaxSeats())\n436: \t\treq.NoteQueued(false)\n437: \t\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.Add(-1)\n438: \t\tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n439: \t}\n440: \treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n441: }\n442: \n443: func (qs *queueSet) IsIdle() bool {\n444: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n445: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n446: \treturn qs.isIdleLocked()\n447: }\n448: \n449: func (qs *queueSet) isIdleLocked() bool {\n450: \treturn qs.totRequestsWaiting == 0 && qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0\n451: }\n452: \n453: // lockAndSyncTime acquires the lock and updates the virtual time.\n454: // Doing them together avoids the mistake of modifying some queue state\n455: // before calling syncTimeLocked.\n456: func (qs *queueSet) lockAndSyncTime(ctx context.Context) {\n457: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n458: \tqs.syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n459: }\n460: \n461: // syncTimeLocked updates the virtual time based on the assumption\n462: // that the current state of the queues has been in effect since\n463: // `qs.lastRealTime`.  Thus, it should be invoked after acquiring the\n464: // lock and before modifying the state of any queue.\n465: func (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n466: \trealNow := qs.clock.Now()\n467: \ttimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n468: \tqs.lastRealTime = realNow\n469: \tprevR := qs.currentR\n470: \tincrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n471: \tqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n472: \tswitch {\n473: \tcase prevR > qs.currentR:\n474: \t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queueset::currentR overflow\"), \"Overflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", realNow.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"prevR\", prevR, \"incrR\", incrR, \"currentR\", qs.currentR)\n475: \tcase qs.currentR >= highR:\n476: \t\tqs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n477: \t}\n478: \tmetrics.SetCurrentR(qs.qCfg.Name, qs.currentR.ToFloat())\n479: }\n480: \n481: // rDecrement is the amount by which the progress meter R is wound backwards\n482: // when needed to avoid overflow.\n483: const rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\n484: \n485: // highR is the threshold that triggers advance of the epoch.\n486: // That is, decrementing the global progress meter R by rDecrement.\n487: const highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n488: \n489: // advanceEpoch subtracts rDecrement from the global progress meter R\n490: // and all the readings that have been taked from that meter.\n491: // The now and incrR parameters are only used to add info to the log messages.\n492: func (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n493: \toldR := qs.currentR\n494: \tqs.currentR -= rDecrement\n495: \tklog.InfoS(\"Advancing epoch\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", now.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"oldR\", oldR, \"newR\", qs.currentR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n496: \tsuccess := true\n497: \tfor qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n498: \t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n499: \t\t\t// Do not just decrement, the value could be quite outdated.\n500: \t\t\t// It is safe to reset to zero in this case, because the next request\n501: \t\t\t// will overwrite the zero with `qs.currentR`.\n502: \t\t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = 0\n503: \t\t\tcontinue\n504: \t\t}\n505: \t\toldNextDispatchR := queue.nextDispatchR\n506: \t\tqueue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n507: \t\tif queue.nextDispatchR > oldNextDispatchR {\n508: \t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queue::nextDispatchR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"oldNextDispatchR\", oldNextDispatchR, \"newNextDispatchR\", queue.nextDispatchR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n509: \t\t\tsuccess = false\n510: \t\t}\n511: \t\tqueue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n512: \t\t\toldArrivalR := req.arrivalR\n513: \t\t\treq.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n514: \t\t\tif req.arrivalR > oldArrivalR {\n515: \t\t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"request::arrivalR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"request\", *req, \"oldArrivalR\", oldArrivalR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n516: \t\t\t\tsuccess = false\n517: \t\t\t}\n518: \t\t\treturn true\n519: \t\t})\n520: \t}\n521: \tmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)\n522: }\n523: \n524: // getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time has\n525: // been advancing, according to the logic in `doc.go`.\n526: func (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n527: \tactiveQueues := 0\n528: \tseatsRequested := 0\n529: \tfor _, queue := range qs.queues {\n530: \t\t// here we want the sum of the maximum width of the requests in this queue since our\n531: \t\t// goal is to find the maximum rate at which the queue could work.\n532: \t\tseatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n533: \t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n534: \t\t\tactiveQueues++\n535: \t\t}\n536: \t}\n537: \tif activeQueues == 0 {\n538: \t\treturn 0\n539: \t}\n540: \treturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n541: }\n542: \n543: // shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked encapsulates the logic required\n544: // to validate and enqueue a request for the queueSet/QueueSet:\n545: // 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n546: // 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n547: // we are at max queue length\n548: // 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n549: // returns the enqueud request on a successful enqueue\n550: // returns nil in the case that there is no available concurrency or\n551: // the queuelengthlimit has been reached\n552: func (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) *request {\n553: \t// Start with the shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n554: \tqueueIdx := qs.shuffleShardLocked(hashValue, descr1, descr2)\n555: \tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n556: \n557: \tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n558: \n559: \t// Create a request and enqueue\n560: \treq := &request{\n561: \t\tqs:                qs,\n562: \t\tfsName:            fsName,\n563: \t\tflowDistinguisher: flowDistinguisher,\n564: \t\tctx:               ctx,\n565: \t\tdecision:          qs.promiseFactory(nil, ctx, decisionCancel),\n566: \t\tarrivalTime:       qs.clock.Now(),\n567: \t\tarrivalR:          qs.currentR,\n568: \t\tqueue:             queue,\n569: \t\tdescr1:            descr1,\n570: \t\tdescr2:            descr2,\n571: \t\tqueueNoteFn:       queueNoteFn,\n572: \t\tworkEstimate:      qs.completeWorkEstimate(workEstimate),\n573: \t}\n574: \tif ok := qs.rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(req); !ok {\n575: \t\treturn nil\n576: \t}\n577: \tmetrics.ObserveQueueLength(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, queue.requestsWaiting.Length())\n578: \treturn req\n579: }\n580: \n581: // shuffleShardLocked uses shuffle sharding to select a queue index\n582: // using the given hashValue and the shuffle sharding parameters of the queueSet.\n583: func (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardLocked(hashValue uint64, descr1, descr2 interface{}) int {\n584: \tvar backHand [8]int\n585: \t// Deal into a data structure, so that the order of visit below is not necessarily the order of the deal.\n586: \t// This removes bias in the case of flows with overlapping hands.\n587: \thand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\n588: \thandSize := len(hand)\n589: \toffset := qs.enqueues % handSize\n590: \tqs.enqueues++\n591: \tbestQueueIdx := -1\n592: \tminQueueSeatSeconds := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds\n593: \tfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n594: \t\tqueueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n595: \t\tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n596: \t\tqueueSum := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum()\n597: \n598: \t\t// this is the total amount of work in seat-seconds for requests\n599: \t\t// waiting in this queue, we will select the queue with the minimum.\n600: \t\tthisQueueSeatSeconds := queueSum.TotalWorkSum\n601: \t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"QS(%s): For request %#+v %#+v considering queue %d with sum: %#v and %d seats in use, nextDispatchR=%v\", qs.qCfg.Name, descr1, descr2, queueIdx, queueSum, queue.seatsInUse, queue.nextDispatchR)\n602: \t\tif thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n603: \t\t\tminQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n604: \t\t\tbestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n605: \t\t}\n606: \t}\n607: \tif klogV := klog.V(6); klogV.Enabled() {\n608: \t\tchosenQueue := qs.queues[bestQueueIdx]\n609: \t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: For request %#+v %#+v chose queue %d, with sum: %#v & %d seats in use & nextDispatchR=%v\", qs.qCfg.Name, qs.clock.Now().Format(nsTimeFmt), qs.currentR, descr1, descr2, bestQueueIdx, chosenQueue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum(), chosenQueue.seatsInUse, chosenQueue.nextDispatchR)\n610: \t}\n611: \treturn bestQueueIdx\n612: }\n613: \n614: // rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked rejects or enqueues the newly arrived\n615: // request, which has been assigned to a queue.  If up against the\n616: // queue length limit and the concurrency limit then returns false.\n617: // Otherwise enqueues and returns true.\n618: func (qs *queueSet) rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request *request) bool {\n619: \tqueue := request.queue\n620: \tcurQueueLength := queue.requestsWaiting.Length()\n621: \t// rejects the newly arrived request if resource criteria not met\n622: \tif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n623: \t\tcurQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n624: \t\treturn false\n625: \t}\n626: \n627: \tqs.enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n628: \treturn true\n629: }\n630: \n631: // enqueues a request into its queue.\n632: func (qs *queueSet) enqueueToBoundLocked(request *request) {\n633: \tqueue := request.queue\n634: \tnow := qs.clock.Now()\n635: \tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n636: \t\t// the queue\u2019s start R is set to the virtual time.\n637: \t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = qs.currentR\n638: \t\tklogV := klog.V(6)\n639: \t\tif klogV.Enabled() {\n640: \t\t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: initialized queue %d start R due to request %#+v %#+v\", qs.qCfg.Name, now.Format(nsTimeFmt), queue.nextDispatchR, queue.index, request.descr1, request.descr2)\n641: \t\t}\n642: \t}\n643: \trequest.removeFromQueueLocked = queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\n644: \tqs.totRequestsWaiting++\n645: \tqs.totSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\n646: \tmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(request.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, request.fsName, 1)\n647: dispatchSansQueueLocked(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}) *request {\n660: \t// does not call \t\t\trequest.workEstimate, queue.index, queue.nextDispatchR)\n740: \t}\n741: \tqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n742: \treturn true\n743: }\n744: \n745: // canAccommodateSeatsLocked returns true if this queueSet has enough\n746: // seats available to accommodate a request with the given number of seats,\n747: // otherwise it returns false.\n748: func (qs *queueSet) canAccommodateSeatsLocked(seats int) bool {\n749: \tswitch {\n750: \tcase qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 0:\n751: \t\t// This is code for exemption from limitation\n752: \t\treturn true\n753: \tcase seats A queue that can not use all those seats and does\n948: // not go empty accumulates a progresively earlier `virtualStart` compared\n949: // to queues that are using more than they are allocated.\n950: // The following hack addresses the first side of that inequity,\n951: // by insisting that dispatch in the virtual world not precede arrival.\n952: func (qs *queueSet) boundNextDispatchLocked(queue *queue) {\n953: \toldestReqFromMinQueue, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n954: \tif oldestReqFromMinQueue == nil {\n955: \t\treturn\n956: \t}\n957: \tvar virtualStartBound = oldestReqFromMinQueue.arrivalR\n958: \tif queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n959: \t\tif klogV := klog.V(4); i < len(keptQueues); i++ {\n991: \t\tkeptQueues[i].index--\n992: \t}\n993: \treturn keptQueues\n994: }\n995: \n996: func (qs *queueSet) Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump {\n997: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n998: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n999: \td := debug.QueueSetDump{\n1000: \t\tQueues:                     make([]debug.QueueDump, len(qs.queues)),\n1001: \t\tQueuelessExecutingRequests: SetMapReduce(dumpRequest(includeRequestDetails), append1[debug.RequestDump])(qs.requestsExecutingSet),\n1002: \t\tWaiting:                    qs.totRequestsWaiting,\n1003: \t\tExecuting:                  qs.totRequestsExecuting,\n1004: \t\tSeatsInUse:                 qs.totSeatsInUse,\n1005: \t\tSeatsWaiting:               qs.totSeatsWaiting,\n1006: \t\tDispatched:                 qs.totRequestsDispatched,\n1007: \t\tRejected:                   qs.totRequestsRejected,\n1008: \t\tTimedout:                   qs.totRequestsTimedout,\n1009: \t\tCancelled:                  qs.totRequestsCancelled,\n1010: \t}\n1011: \tfor i, q := range qs.queues {\n1012: \t\td.Queues[i] = q.dumpLocked(includeRequestDetails)\n1013: \t}\n1014: \treturn d\n1015: }\n1016: \n1017: func OnRequestDispatched(r fq.Request) {\n1018: \treq, ok := r.(*request)\n1019: \tif !ok {\n1020: \t\treturn\n1021: \t}\n1022: \n1023: \tqs := req.qs\n1024: \tif qs != nil {\n1025: \t\tqs.lock.Lock()\n1026: \t\tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n1027: \t\tqs.totRequestsDispatched++\n1028: \t}\n1029: }\n1030: ",

For a configController, the\\n94: // suffix \\\"ReadLocked\\\" stipulates a read lock while just \\\"Locked\\\"\\n95: // stipulates a full lock.  Absence of either suffix means that either\\n96: // (a) the lock must NOT be held at call time and will not be held\\n97: // upon return or (b) locking is irrelevant.\\n98: \\n99: // StartFunction begins the process of handling a request. %v but should not be less than the lower bound %v\", idx, item.upperBound, item.lowerBound)\n138: \t\t}\n139: \t\tif target < MinTarget {\n140: \t\t\t// tweak this to a non-zero value so avoid dividing by zero\n141: \t\t\ttarget = MinTarget\n142: \t\t}\n143: \t\tlowSum += item.lowerBound\n144: \t\thighSum += item.upperBound\n145: \t\ttargetSum += target\n146: \t\trelativeItem := relativeAllocItem{\n147: \t\t\ttarget:             target,\n148: \t\t\trelativeLowerBound: item.lowerBound / target,\n149: \t\t\trelativeUpperBound: item.upperBound / target,\n150: \t\t}\n151: \t\tubRange.note(relativeItem.relativeUpperBound)\n152: \t\tlbRange.note(relativeItem.relativeLowerBound)\n153: \t\trelativeItems[idx] = relativeItem\n154: \t}\n155: \tif lbRange.max > 1 {\n156: \t\treturn nil, 0, fmt.Errorf(\"lbRange.max-1=%v, which is impossible because lbRange.max can not be greater than 1\", lbRange.max-1)\n157: \t}\n158: \tif lowSum-requiredSumF > epsilon {\n159: \t\treturn nil, 0, fmt.Errorf(\"lower bounds sum to %v, which is higher than the required sum of %v\", lowSum, requiredSum)\n160: \t}\n161: \tif requiredSumF-highSum > epsilon {\n162: \t\treturn nil, 0, fmt.Errorf(\"upper bounds sum to %v, which is lower than the required sum of %v\", highSum, requiredSum)\n163: \t}\n164: \tans := make([]float64, len(classes))\n165: \tif requiredSum == 0 {\n166: \t\treturn ans, 0, nil\n167: \t}\n168: \tif lowSum-requiredSumF > -epsilon { // no wiggle room, constrained from below\n169: \t\tfor idx, item := range classes {\n170: \t\t\tans[idx] = item.lowerBound\n171: \t\t}\n172: \t\treturn ans, lbRange.min, nil\n173: \t}\n174: \tif requiredSumF-highSum > -epsilon { // no wiggle room, constrained from above\n175: \t\tfor idx, item := range classes {\n176: \t\t\tans[idx] = item.upperBound\n177: \t\t}\n178: \t\treturn ans, ubRange.max, nil\n179: \t}\n180: \t// Now we know the solution is a unique fairProp in [lbRange.min, ubRange.max].\n181: \t// See if the solution does not run into any bounds.\n182: \tfairProp := requiredSumF / targetSum\n183: \tif lbRange.max <= fairProp && fairProp <= ubRange.min { // no bounds matter\n184: \t\tfor idx := range classes {\n185: \t\t\tans[idx] = relativeItems[idx].target * fairProp\n186: \t\t}\n187: \t\treturn ans, fairProp, nil\n188: \t}\n189: \t// Sadly, some bounds matter.\n190: \t// We find the solution by sorting the bounds and considering progressively\n191: \t// higher values of fairProp, starting from lbRange.min.\n192: \trap := (&relativeAllocProblem{items: relativeItems}).initIndices()\n193: \tsumSoFar := lowSum\n194: \tfairProp = lbRange.min\n195: \tvar sensitiveTargetSum, deltaSensitiveTargetSum float64\n196: \tvar numSensitiveClasses, deltaSensitiveClasses int\n197: \tvar nextIdx int\n198: \t// `nextIdx` is the next `rap` index to consider.\n199: \t// `sumSoFar` is what the allocs would sum to if the current\n200: \t// value of `fairProp` solves the problem.\n201: \t// If the current value of fairProp were the answer then\n202: \t// `sumSoFar == requiredSum`.\n203: \t// Otherwise the next increment in fairProp involves changing the allocations\n204: \t// of `numSensitiveClasses` classes whose targets sum to `sensitiveTargetSum`;\n205: \t// for the other classes, an upper or lower bound has applied and will continue to apply.\n206: \t// The last increment of nextIdx calls for adding `deltaSensitiveClasses`\n207: \t// to `numSensitiveClasses` and adding `deltaSensitiveTargetSum` to `sensitiveTargetSum`.\n208: \tfor sumSoFar < requiredSumF {\n209: \t\t// There might be more than one bound that is equal to the current value\n210: \t\t// of fairProp; find all of them because they will all be relevant to\n211: \t\t// the next change in fairProp.\n212: \t\t// Set nextBound to the next bound that is NOT equal to fairProp,\n213: \t\t// and advance nextIdx to the index of that bound.\n214: \t\tvar nextBound float64\n215: \t\tfor {\n216: \t\t\tsensitiveTargetSum += deltaSensitiveTargetSum\n217: \t\t\tnumSensitiveClasses += deltaSensitiveClasses\n218: \t\t\tif nextIdx >= rap.Len() {\n219: \t\t\t\treturn nil, 0, fmt.Errorf(\"impossible: ran out of bounds to consider in bound-constrained problem\")\n220: \t\t\t}\n221: \t\t\tvar itemIdx int\n222: \t\t\tvar lower bool\n223: \t\t\tnextBound, itemIdx, lower = rap.decode(nextIdx)\n224: \t\t\tif lower {\n225: \t\t\t\tdeltaSensitiveClasses = 1\n226: \t\t\t\tdeltaSensitiveTargetSum = rap.items[itemIdx].target\n227: \t\t\t} else {\n228: \t\t\t\tdeltaSensitiveClasses = -1\n229: \t\t\t\tdeltaSensitiveTargetSum = -rap.items[itemIdx].target\n230: \t\t\t}\n231: \t\t\tnextIdx++\n232: \t\t\tif nextBound > fairProp {\n233: \t\t\t\tbreak\n234: \t\t\t}\n235: \t\t}\n236: \t\t// fairProp can increase to nextBound without passing any intermediate bounds.\n237: \t\tif numSensitiveClasses == 0 {\n238: \t\t\t// No deckSize).\n75: // For example, for deckSize=128 and handSize=4 this function might call pick(14); pick(73); pick(119); pick(26).\n76: func (d *Dealer) Deal(hashValue uint64, pick func(int)) {\n77: \t// 15 is the largest possible value of handSize\n78: \tvar remainders [15]int\n79: \n80: \tfor i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n81: \t\thashValueNext := hashValue / uint64(d.deckSize-i)\n82: \t\tremainders[i] = int(hashValue - uint64(d.deckSize-i)*hashValueNext)\n83: \t\thashValue = hashValueNext\n84: \t}\n85: \n86: \tfor i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n87: \t\tcard := remainders[i]\n88: \t\tfor j := i; j > 0; j-- {\n89: \t\t\tif card >= remainders[j-1] {\n90: \t\t\t\tcard++\n91: \t\t\t}\n92: \t\t}\n93: \t\tpick(card)\n94: \t}\n95: }\n96: \n97: // DealIntoHand shuffles and deals according to the Dealer's parameters,\n98: // using the given hashValue as the source of entropy and then\n99: // returns the dealt cards as a slice of `int`.\n100: // If `hand` has the correct length as Dealer's handSize, it will be used as-is and no allocations will be made.\n101: // If `hand` is nil or too small, it will be extended (performing an allocation).\n102: // If `hand` is too large, a sub-slice will be returned.\n103: func (d *Dealer) DealIntoHand(hashValue uint64, hand []int) []int {\n104: \th := hand[:0]\n105: \td.Deal(hashValue, func(card int) { h = append(h, card) })\n106: \treturn h\n107: }\n108: ",

31. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem implements fair multi-tenant queuing for the Kubernetes API server. Its core responsibility is to ensure that no single client or workload monopolizes API server capacity\u2014even under heavy load\u2014while still providing guaranteed minimum throughput and bounded latency to every priority class.\n\nThe subsystem is the realization of the \"Fair Queuing for Server Requests\" algorithm described in [KEP-1040](https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md). It adapts the classic WFQ (Weighted Fair Queuing) technique to a stateless, per-request server context, replacing per-byte cost accounting with per-seat-second cost accounting.\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream (what feeds the QueueSet):**\n\n- The `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) classifies each incoming request against an ordered list of `FlowSchema` objects, selects a matching `PriorityLevelConfiguration`, computes a flow distinguisher hash, estimates work, and calls `QueueSet.StartRequest`.\n- The HTTP filter entry point is `configController.Handle` (`apf_filter.go:155`), which is invoked by the API server's handler chain for every non-exempt request.\n\n**Downstream (what the QueueSet controls):**\n\n- The `execFn` callback passed to `Handle` \u2014 the actual request handler. The QueueSet decides whether to call it, delay it (queued wait), or suppress it (reject).\n\n**Peer dependencies:**\n\n| Component | Location | Role |\n|-----------|----------|------|\n| `shufflesharding.Dealer` | `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` | Deterministic queue selection |\n| `promise.WriteOnce` | `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go` | Cross-goroutine dispatch signaling |\n| `eventclock.Interface` | `fairqueuing/eventclock/` | Mockable wall clock + deferred callbacks |\n| Work estimators | `flowcontrol/request/` | Seat count computation per request |\n| `metrics` package | `flowcontrol/metrics/` | Prometheus instrumentation |\n| `Integrator` | `fairqueuing/integrator.go` | Time-weighted seat-demand statistics |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `configController` \u2014 Configuration and Classification Layer\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`\n\nThe `configController` struct is the long-lived controller that:\n\n1. Watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API objects via informers and rebuilds the in-memory routing table whenever they change (`syncOne` \u2192 `digestConfigObjects` \u2192 `lockAndDigestConfigObjects`).\n2. Classifies every incoming request: iterates `cfgCtlr.flowSchemas` (sorted by ascending numerical `MatchingPrecedence`) and calls `matchesFlowSchema` until a match is found. The mandatory `catch-all` schema is always last, so no request goes unclassified (`startRequest`, line 1022).\n3. Derives the `flowDistinguisher` string from the matched FlowSchema's `DistinguisherMethod` (either the user name or the namespace), then computes a 64-bit hash via SHA-256 (`hashFlowID`, line 1131).\n4. Invokes `WorkEstimatorFunc` to get a `WorkEstimate` for the request (seats and optional additional latency).\n5. Delegates to `priorityLevelState.queues.StartRequest(...)` for admission and queuing.\n6. Runs a periodic borrowing rebalancer (`updateBorrowing`, every `borrowingAdjustmentPeriod` = 10 seconds) to dynamically redistribute unused concurrency across priority levels.\n\n**`priorityLevelState`** (line 202) ties together a `QueueSet`, the API object that configures it, the current concurrency limits (`nominalCL`, `minCL`, `maxCL`, `currentCL`), and a `seatDemandIntegrator` that accumulates demand statistics.\n\n### 2.2 `QueueSetFactory` / `QueueSetCompleter` \u2014 Two-Phase Construction\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/interface.go`, `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\nConstruction is split into two phases to allow configuration validation before committing to a concurrency slot:\n\n```\nQueueSetFactory.BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, ...) \u2192 QueueSetCompleter\nQueueSetCompleter.Complete(DispatchingConfig)         \u2192 QueueSet\n```\n\nThis matters because the `DispatchingConfig.ConcurrencyLimit` is computed by the borrowing algorithm after the `QueuingConfig` is already validated. The same two-phase pattern applies to reconfiguration (`QueueSet.BeginConfigChange`).\n\nOn `Complete`, the `queueSetCompleter` either constructs a new `queueSet` struct or reconfigures an existing one via `setConfiguration`, which:\n- Adds queues if `DesiredNumQueues` increased (existing queues drain via attrition, never forcibly removed).\n- Sets metric denominators.\n- Calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` immediately, so newly available capacity is used right away.\n\n### 2.3 `queueSet` \u2014 The Core Fair-Queuing Engine\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\n`queueSet` is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`. All methods that require the lock use the `Locked` suffix convention. The struct tracks:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `queues []*queue` | The array of per-flow virtual queues |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Global virtual-time progress meter R |\n| `lastRealTime time.Time` | Wall clock snapshot when R was last updated |\n| `robinIndex int` | Round-robin cursor for dispatch selection |\n| `totSeatsInUse int` | Current seat occupancy (used vs. `dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit`) |\n| `totRequestsWaiting int` | Count of queued-but-not-dispatched requests |\n| `dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer` | Queue selection engine |\n\n### 2.4 `queue` \u2014 Per-Flow Virtual Queue\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting   fifo               // FIFO list of waiting requests\n    nextDispatchR     SeatSeconds        // virtual clock: next dispatch time for this queue\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request] // currently executing requests\n    index             int                // position in queueSet.queues\n    seatsInUse        int                // seats occupied by executing requests\n}\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` is the core state for the WFQ algorithm: it advances by `totalWork` every time a request is dispatched from this queue, creating a virtual start time for the next request. This is what enforces per-queue fair share.\n\n### 2.5 `request` \u2014 Per-Request Tracking Object\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\nEach request carries:\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate` \u2014 initial seats \u00d7 estimated duration + final seats \u00d7 additional latency\n- `arrivalR SeatSeconds` \u2014 the value of `currentR` when the request arrived; used for the anti-windup bound\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 the dispatch/cancel decision, communicated from the dispatch goroutine to the waiting goroutine without the lock\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc` \u2014 O(1) removal from the FIFO list\n\n### 2.6 `fifo` / `requestFIFO` \u2014 Per-Queue FIFO List\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go`\n\nA standard `container/list.List` wrapper with an incrementally maintained `queueSum` (sum of `InitialSeats`, `MaxSeats`, and `totalWork` for all waiting requests). This allows O(1) aggregate queries used in both shuffle sharding and dispatch decisions.\n\n### 2.7 `promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 Dispatch Signaling\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\nA write-once, thread-safe value container. The `Get` method blocks until either:\n- `Set(decisionExecute)` is called (by the dispatcher, under the lock), or\n- The request's `context.Context` is cancelled (context deadline/cancellation propagates as `decisionCancel`).\n\nThis allows the waiting goroutine in `request.wait()` to block outside the lock while the dispatch goroutine operates under the lock.\n\n### 2.8 Work Estimators\n\n**Files:** `request/width.go`, `request/list_work_estimator.go`, `request/mutating_work_estimator.go`, `request/config.go`\n\nThe `WorkEstimator` maps HTTP verbs to seat estimates:\n\n- **Read-only non-list (get, watch without init events):** 1 seat (`MinimumSeats = 1`)\n- **List / watch with init events:** `ceil(estimatedObjects / objectsPerSeat)` seats (default: 1 seat per 100 objects), bounded by `MaximumListSeatsLimit` (default: 10, or 100 with `SizeBasedListCostEstimate` feature gate)\n- **Mutating (create/update/patch/delete):** 1 `InitialSeat` + optional `FinalSeats = ceil(watchCount / watchesPerSeat)` (default: 1 seat per 10 watches), with `AdditionalLatency` to model the cost of fan-out to watch handlers\n\nThe **two-phase seat model** is key: `InitialSeats` are held during the main body of request execution; `FinalSeats` (at a potentially different, usually smaller, count) are held for `AdditionalLatency` after the handler returns, representing the cost of dispatching change notifications to watch goroutines. This is deferred via `clock.EventAfterDuration` so it has no impact on client-observed latency.\n\n### 2.9 `shufflesharding.Dealer` \u2014 Queue Selection\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`\n\nThe `Dealer` implements a deterministic \"dealing a hand from a deck\" algorithm. Given a hash value and deck/hand sizes, it uses successive modulo extraction to produce a pseudo-random hand of `handSize` distinct queue indices from a deck of `deckSize` queues:\n\n```\nremainders[i] = hashValue mod (deckSize - i)\nhashValue     = hashValue / (deckSize - i)\n```\n\nThen a Fisher-Yates-like reconstruction maps remainders to actual indices. This uses `ceil(handSize \u00d7 log\u2082(deckSize))` bits of entropy, bounded by `MaxHashBits = 60`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Arrival: Classification and Hashing\n\n```\nHTTP request arrives at API server\n  \u2192 apf_filter.go: configController.Handle(ctx, requestDigest, ...)\n    \u2192 configController.startRequest(ctx, rd, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn)\n      \u2192 iterate cfgCtlr.flowSchemas (sorted by MatchingPrecedence)\n        \u2192 rule.go: matchesFlowSchema(rd, fs)  [subject + resource/nonResource rules]\n      \u2192 computeFlowDistinguisher(rd, fs.Spec.DistinguisherMethod)\n        \u2192 user name OR namespace\n      \u2192 hashFlowID(fsName, flowDistinguisher)  [SHA-256 \u2192 uint64]\n      \u2192 workEstimator()  [called here, result passed to StartRequest]\n      \u2192 plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n```\n\nThe `flowDistinguisher` determines which \"flow\" this request belongs to. Two requests from the same user (distinguisher = user name) or in the same namespace (distinguisher = namespace) map to the same flow, and thus are likely to land in the same queue via shuffle sharding\u2014enabling per-flow isolation.\n\n### 3.2 Queue Assignment: Shuffle Sharding\n\nInside `StartRequest` (`queueset.go:308`), if `DesiredNumQueues >= 1`, the request goes through `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`:\n\n```\nshuffleShardLocked(hashValue, ...)\n  \u2192 dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])   // deals handSize queue indices\n  \u2192 offset = qs.enqueues % handSize               // staggered starting position (anti-bias)\n  \u2192 for each queue in hand:\n      thisQueueSeatSeconds = queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n      track minimum\n  \u2192 return bestQueueIdx  (minimum total waiting work)\n```\n\nThe shuffle-sharding property: with `handSize = 8` out of `deckSize = 128` queues, the probability that two distinct flows share all 8 queues is `(8/128)^8 \u2248 10^{-10}`. Even a noisy neighbor running thousands of requests can only fill 8 queues; the other flow's 8 queues will almost certainly include some with lower occupancy, limiting blast radius.\n\nThe **minimum-work selection** (not minimum-length) within the dealt hand means a queue with few but large requests is still preferred over a queue with many small ones\u2014proportional to actual resource cost.\n\n### 3.3 Reject or Enqueue\n\n`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` (`queueset.go:618`) enforces:\n\n```\nif totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit:\n    return false  // reject: full queue + full concurrency\n```\n\nNote the **AND** condition: a queue that is full can still accept requests if there is remaining concurrency. Only when *both* limits are hit is the request rejected with a `queue-full` metric tag.\n\n`enqueueToBoundLocked` (`queueset.go:632`) adds the request to the FIFO list, initializes `queue.nextDispatchR = currentR` if the queue was empty (so a fresh queue doesn't inherit a stale virtual start time), and updates all counters and metrics atomically.\n\n### 3.4 Dispatch: Virtual Time and Round-Robin Selection\n\nAfter enqueue, `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs a loop:\n\n```\nwhile totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit:\n    dispatchLocked()\n```\n\n`dispatchLocked` calls `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` which scans all queues in **round-robin order** (advancing `robinIndex` by 1 each iteration) and selects the queue whose head request has the **minimum virtual finish time**:\n\n```\nvirtualFinish(queue) = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\nThis is the FIFO WFQ criterion: the queue that would finish soonest in the virtual world goes next. Among ties, the round-robin ordering provides an implicit secondary sort.\n\n**Concurrency check before dispatch:**\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) canAccommodateSeatsLocked(seats int) bool {\n    if seats > ConcurrencyLimit && totRequestsExecuting == 0:\n        return true   // oversized request: allow only when server is empty\n    return totSeatsInUse + seats <= ConcurrencyLimit\n}\n```\n\nIf the head of the selected queue cannot be accommodated, `dispatchLocked` returns `false` and the loop stops. No other queue is tried \u2014 the system waits for running requests to complete and free seats.\n\n**Post-dispatch accounting** (`queueset.go:741`):\n\n```go\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n```\n\nThis is the heart of the WFQ algorithm: after dispatching, the queue's virtual clock advances by the request's work, making it \"more expensive\" relative to other queues and ensuring it will not be selected again until the others catch up.\n\n### 3.5 Waiting: The `promise.WriteOnce` Pattern\n\nThe client goroutine (the HTTP handler goroutine) returns from `StartRequest` with a non-nil `fq.Request` and calls `req.Finish(execFn)`. Internally this calls `req.wait()` which blocks on `req.decision.Get()`. This call releases the per-goroutine stack into a channel select:\n\n```go\nfunc (p *promise) Get() interface{} {\n    select {\n    case <-p.setCh:           // dispatch goroutine called Set(decisionExecute)\n    case <-p.doneCtx.Done(): // request context cancelled (timeout)\n        p.Set(p.doneVal)      // doneVal = decisionCancel\n    }\n    return p.value\n}\n```\n\nThis design ensures the waiting goroutine never holds the `queueSet.lock` while blocking. When the request's context expires, `decisionCancel` is set and `request.wait()` removes the request from its queue, decrements counters, and records a `time-out` metric (`queueset.go:427\u2013438`).\n\n### 3.6 Execution and Completion\n\nOn `decisionExecute`, `Finish` calls `execFn()` \u2014 the real HTTP handler. On return, `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible` is called:\n\n1. **`finishRequestLocked`** (`queueset.go:863`):\n   - Decrements `totRequestsExecuting`.\n   - Removes request from `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n   - **Adjusts `queue.nextDispatchR`** for actual vs. estimated service time:\n     ```go\n     queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(float64(r.InitialSeats()), estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n     ```\n     If the request ran *faster* than `estimatedServiceDuration` (default: 3ms), `nextDispatchR` is *moved earlier*, crediting the queue; if slower, it moves later \u2014 a soft real-time feedback loop.\n   - If `AdditionalLatency > 0`, defers `releaseSeatsLocked` via `clock.EventAfterDuration`, then calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` again from the deferred callback.\n\n2. **`removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`**: If the queue is now empty and the total queue count exceeds `DesiredNumQueues`, the queue is removed and `robinIndex` is adjusted.\n\n3. **`boundNextDispatchLocked`** (anti-windup): Ensures `queue.nextDispatchR` never falls below the `arrivalR` of the oldest waiting request. Without this, a queue that received small requests and finished them quickly would accumulate a very early `nextDispatchR`, creating an unfair advantage.\n\n### 3.7 Virtual Time Synchronization\n\n`syncTimeLocked` is called every time the lock is acquired (`lockAndSyncTime`). It advances `currentR` based on elapsed real time and the current virtual time ratio:\n\n```go\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\n`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked` computes:\n\n```go\nratio = min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nwhere `seatsRequested` is the sum over all queues of `(seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum of waiting requests)`. This ratio equals the number of seat-seconds allocated per queue per second. When no queues are active, the ratio is zero and `currentR` freezes.\n\n**Epoch management** (`advanceEpoch`): When `currentR` approaches `MaxSeatSeconds/2`, all queue `nextDispatchR` values and request `arrivalR` values are decremented by `MaxSeatSeconds/2` to prevent overflow. This is an O(N) operation proportional to the number of queues and waiting requests.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Borrowing Algorithm: Dynamic Concurrency Reallocation\n\nThe `configController` runs `updateBorrowing` every 10 seconds to redistibute unused concurrency across priority levels. This is layered above the per-`QueueSet` dispatch and uses seat demand statistics tracked by the `Integrator`.\n\n**Seat demand stats** (`priorityLevelState.seatDemandStats`):\n- The `Integrator` (`fairqueuing/integrator.go`) tracks the time-integral of `totSeatsInUse + totSeatsWaiting` as a continuous function, computing mean, standard deviation, and high watermark over each adjustment period.\n- `envelope = avg + stdDev` estimates a \"typical peak\".\n- `smoothed = max(envelope, A*smoothed + (1-A)*envelope)` with decay coefficient `A = 0.977` (half-life \u2248 5 minutes) prevents oscillation.\n\n**`computeConcurrencyAllocation`** (`conc_alloc.go:119`) solves a bounded proportional allocation problem:\n\n- **Inputs:** each priority level's `target = max(minCurrentCL, smoothed demand)`, `lowerBound = minCL`, `upperBound = maxCL`.\n- **Constraint:** sum of allocations = `nominalCLSum`.\n- **Algorithm:** find a single scalar `fairProp` such that `alloc[i] = clamp(fairProp \u00d7 target[i], lower[i], upper[i])` and the allocations sum correctly. This is solved by sorting the bounds and scanning linearly \u2014 O(N log N) per adjustment cycle.\n\nEach priority level's `currentCL` is set to the allocation result, and `plState.qsCompleter.Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL, ...})` is called, which calls `setConfiguration` on the `queueSet`, immediately triggering `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`.\n\n**Config limits that feed borrowing:**\n- `NominalConcurrencyShares`: proportional weight in the initial allocation.\n- `LendablePercent`: what fraction of nominal can be lent to others. `minCL = nominalCL \u00d7 (1 - lendablePercent/100)`.\n- `BorrowingLimitPercent`: how much above nominal can be borrowed. `maxCL = nominalCL \u00d7 (1 + borrowingLimitPercent/100)`.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Rejection Under Load\n\nThere are two rejection paths:\n\n1. **No-queue mode** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`): immediate reject if `totSeatsInUse + MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`. Used for priority levels configured with `LimitResponse.Type: Reject`.\n2. **Queue-full**: rejected if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`. The AND condition means a full queue is *not* sufficient alone \u2014 there must also be no available concurrency. This is intentional: it avoids rejecting requests that could be dispatched immediately if concurrency were available.\n\nRejected requests get metric tag `\"queue-full\"` or `\"concurrency-limit\"` via `metrics.AddReject`.\n\n### 5.2 Context Cancellation / Timeout\n\nWhen a request's context is cancelled while waiting, `promise.Get` unblocks via `<-p.doneCtx.Done()` and `decisionCancel` is set. The `wait()` method then calls `removeFromQueueLocked()` to atomically remove the request and update all counters, including `boundNextDispatchLocked` to re-check the anti-windup bound on the now-modified queue head.\n\nThe double-decrement protection (checking `e.Value == nil` in the `removeFromFIFOFunc` closure) ensures idempotent removal even if the request was concurrently dispatched.\n\n### 5.3 Oversized Requests (seats > ConcurrencyLimit)\n\n`canAccommodateSeatsLocked` (`queueset.go:748`) has a special case: if a single request's `MaxSeats` exceeds `ConcurrencyLimit`, it is allowed to execute only when the server is completely idle (`totRequestsExecuting == 0`). This prevents starvation of such requests but causes them to block all other dispatches until they complete. A log warning is emitted if `totalWork > rDecrement/100`.\n\nAdditionally, at dispatch time, if `FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`, `FinalSeats` is clamped to `ConcurrencyLimit` and `AdditionalLatency` is scaled up proportionally to preserve total work:\n\n```go\nadditionalLatency = finalWork.DurationPerSeat(float64(finalSeats))\n```\n\n### 5.4 Tradeoffs in the Virtual Time Model\n\n**All non-empty queues advance at the same rate.** `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked` divides available capacity equally among active queues, regardless of their actual seat demand. A queue with one thin request and a queue with ten fat requests both get the same virtual time increment. This is correct for isolation (each active flow gets a fair share), but can cause suboptimal dispatch ordering when seat demands are heterogeneous.\n\n**Estimated service duration is fixed** at `3 * time.Millisecond` (set in `Complete`). This constant interacts with `nextDispatchR` adjustment: if actual service is systematically much shorter or longer, the anti-windup bounds may be loose. There is no feedback from real latency into the estimate itself.\n\n**The round-robin tie-breaking** in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` means that if all queues have the same `virtualFinish`, the queue just after the last dispatched queue wins. This provides a weak fairness guarantee when work estimates are equal but does not track actual byte throughput.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 6.1 `promiseFactoryFactory` \u2014 Testability Hook\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\nInjected via `newTestableQueueSetFactory`. In production this always returns `promise.NewWriteOnce`. Tests substitute a factory that records or controls dispatch signals. Misuse in production (e.g., a blocking factory) would deadlock the dispatch goroutine.\n\n### 6.2 `eventclock.Interface` \u2014 Clock Abstraction\n\n`queueSet.clock` is an `eventclock.Interface`, not the standard `time.Now`. This allows tests to advance virtual time and trigger `EventAfterDuration` callbacks without sleeping. Replacing this in production with a slow or faulty clock would corrupt all virtual time calculations.\n\n### 6.3 `WorkEstimatorFunc` \u2014 Pluggable Cost Model\n\n`NewWorkEstimator` in `request/width.go` is called from the APF filter and returns a `WorkEstimatorFunc`. It is structured as a composable function (not an interface), making it easy to replace the entire cost function or wrap it with a decorator. The cost model directly affects both scheduling fairness and the anti-starvation behavior for wide requests.\n\n**Risks:**\n- Underestimating list cost (e.g., for aggregated APIs where `ObjectCountNotFoundErr` returns `minSeats = 1`) means such requests occupy fewer virtual queue slots, potentially giving them an unfair advantage.\n- Overestimating watch fan-out cost blocks dispatching other requests while the queue accumulates enough seats to accommodate the wide request.\n\n### 6.4 `QueueSetFactory` Interface \u2014 Queuing Backend Replacement\n\nThe `configController` depends only on the `fq.QueueSetFactory` interface (`fairqueuing/interface.go`), injected at construction. An alternative fair-queuing backend (e.g., one with per-priority weighted scheduling or a deficit round-robin variant) could be injected without changing the controller logic. The interface contract is minimal: `BeginConstruction`, `Complete`, `StartRequest`, `Finish`, `IsIdle`, `Dump`.\n\n### 6.5 `MaxSeatsTracker` \u2014 Per-Priority-Level Seat Caps\n\n`MaxSeatsTracker` (`apf_controller.go:157`) tracks per-priority-level max seats used by the work estimator. It is set in `finishQueueSetReconfigsLocked` (`line 892`):\n\n```go\nmaxSeats = MAX(1, MIN(0.15 \u00d7 nominalCL, nominalCL / handSize))\n```\n\nThis ensures the max seats cap scales with the priority level's concurrency allocation, preventing a single list request from consuming more than 15% of a level's concurrency. Changing `priorityLevelMaxSeatsPercent` from its current `0.15` would shift the balance between large-request throughput and multi-tenant fairness.\n\n### 6.6 FlowSchema and Priority Level Config \u2014 Operator Customization\n\nOperators customize APF behavior exclusively through Kubernetes API objects:\n- `FlowSchema.Spec.Rules` \u2014 what requests match, with what distinguisher\n- `PriorityLevelConfiguration.Spec.Limited.LimitResponse.Queuing` \u2014 `Queues`, `QueueLengthLimit`, `HandSize`\n- `NominalConcurrencyShares`, `LendablePercent`, `BorrowingLimitPercent`\n\n**Risk:** Setting `HandSize` close to `Queues` (e.g., `HandSize = Queues`) eliminates the shuffle-sharding isolation benefit: every flow sees all queues, and a noisy neighbor can fill them all. Setting `HandSize = 1` is pure hashing (no election among candidates), breaking the \"choose best of hand\" anti-noisy-neighbor property. The sweet spot for defaults (e.g., `HandSize = 8, Queues = 128`) provides `(8/128)^8 \u2248 10^{-10}` collision probability.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance\n\n**Lock contention:** All QueueSet state is guarded by a single `sync.Mutex`. Under high request rates, this mutex is acquired and released for every `StartRequest`, every dispatch cycle, and every `finishRequestLocked`. The lock is held briefly (no I/O, no slow computation inside), but at very high concurrency (thousands of RPS per priority level) contention may become visible. The `configController`'s `lock.RLock()` during `startRequest` is separate and allows concurrent classification reads.\n\n**`syncTimeLocked` on every lock acquisition:** Every call to `lockAndSyncTime` advances virtual time. This is O(1) arithmetic. However, if `advanceEpoch` is triggered (every ~2^63 seat-nanoseconds of accumulated work at scale), it is O(queues \u00d7 waitingRequests). This should be extremely rare in practice.\n\n**`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` loop:** In the worst case (many queues, many requests), each `dispatchLocked` call scans all queues via round-robin. O(numQueues) per dispatch. With `Queues = 128` and `ConcurrencyLimit = 400`, the loop runs at most 400 times per invocation, touching 128 queues each time: 51,200 iterations per fully-loaded dispatch cycle. This is bounded and predictable.\n\n### 7.2 Reliability\n\n**Mandatory FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations:** `imaginePL` (`apf_controller.go:991`) synthesizes the mandatory `exempt` and `catch-all` objects if they are absent from the API, ensuring the system is never stuck with an unclassified request. Deleting these objects is recoverable because the controller will re-create them (in memory) on the next sync.\n\n**Quiescing priority levels:** When a PLC is deleted, its `priorityLevelState.quiescing` is set to true. The QueueSet continues to drain. Only after `queues.IsIdle()` is confirmed does the controller trigger a config reload that removes the state. This prevents requests already queued against a deleted level from being abruptly cancelled.\n\n**Double-dispatch prevention:** `promise.WriteOnce` uses `sync.Once` to ensure `Set` is idempotent. If a request's context fires and `decisionCancel` is set while `dispatchLocked` simultaneously calls `Set(decisionExecute)`, only the first write wins. The dispatch loop detects the lost race via `!request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)` and continues without changing seat counts (the request is no longer in the queue but never entered `executing` state).\n\n**FlowSchema status update rate limiting:** `shouldDelayUpdate` tracks how often each FlowSchema has had its status updated. If the same schema is updated more than 5 times in a minute, subsequent updates are delayed by a random 30\u201375 second jitter to prevent thundering-herd status updates when many apiservers are reconciling simultaneously.\n\n### 7.3 Maintainability\n\n**The `Locked` naming convention** is strictly enforced in the queueset package: every method that requires `qs.lock` held has the `Locked` suffix, and `ToBoundLocked` signals that `boundNextDispatchLocked` must be called afterward. Violating this convention would introduce subtle data races.\n\n**Metrics integration is pervasive.** Every state transition (enqueue, dispatch, reject, finish, seat change) updates Prometheus gauges and counters. The `seatDemandIntegrator` provides continuous time-weighted statistics for the borrowing algorithm. Missing a metric update in a new code path would silently corrupt the borrowing decisions.\n\n**The config digest is all-or-nothing:** `lockAndDigestConfigObjects` reads all FlowSchemas and PLCs at once and atomically replaces `cfgCtlr.flowSchemas` and `cfgCtlr.priorityLevelStates`. Partial updates are not possible. This simplifies reasoning but means any validation error for one object (e.g., a bad HandSize) causes that object to be dropped from the active config entirely, not just flagged.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go` | HTTP handler entry point: `Interface`, `New`, `Handle` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go` | Main controller: config digestion, borrowing, request classification, `startRequest` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/conc_alloc.go` | Bounded proportional allocation algorithm for borrowing |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/rule.go` | FlowSchema matching logic (subjects, resources, non-resources) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/watch_tracker.go` | Watch registration tracking for mutating work estimator |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` | `QueueSet`, `QueueSetFactory`, `QueuingConfig`, `DispatchingConfig` interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/integrator.go` | Time-weighted statistical integrator (demand tracking) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | Core WFQ engine: `StartRequest`, dispatch loop, virtual time |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | `request`, `queue`, `queueSum`, `completedWorkEstimate` types |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` | FIFO list with incremental `queueSum` aggregation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go` | Write-once, context-cancellable dispatch signal |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go` | `WorkEstimate` type and top-level `NewWorkEstimator` dispatcher |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/list_work_estimator.go` | Seat estimation for list/watch requests (object-count and size-based) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/mutating_work_estimator.go` | Seat estimation for mutating requests (watch fan-out cost) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/seat_seconds.go` | Fixed-point `SeatSeconds` arithmetic type |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/config.go` | `WorkEstimatorConfig` and defaults (1 seat/100 objects, 1 seat/10 watches) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` | Shuffle-sharding dealer: deterministic hand-from-deck dealing |\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
