{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem implements fair multi-tenant queuing for the Kubernetes API server. Its core responsibility is to ensure that no single client or workload monopolizes API server capacity\u2014even under heavy load\u2014while still providing guaranteed minimum throughput and bounded latency to every priority class.\n\nThe subsystem is the realization of the \"Fair Queuing for Server Requests\" algorithm described in [KEP-1040](https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md). It adapts the classic WFQ (Weighted Fair Queuing) technique to a stateless, per-request server context, replacing per-byte cost accounting with per-seat-second cost accounting.\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream (what feeds the QueueSet):**\n\n- The `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) classifies each incoming request against an ordered list of `FlowSchema` objects, selects a matching `PriorityLevelConfiguration`, computes a flow distinguisher hash, estimates work, and calls `QueueSet.StartRequest`.\n- The HTTP filter entry point is `configController.Handle` (`apf_filter.go:155`), which is invoked by the API server's handler chain for every non-exempt request.\n\n**Downstream (what the QueueSet controls):**\n\n- The `execFn` callback passed to `Handle` \u2014 the actual request handler. The QueueSet decides whether to call it, delay it (queued wait), or suppress it (reject).\n\n**Peer dependencies:**\n\n| Component | Location | Role |\n|-----------|----------|------|\n| `shufflesharding.Dealer` | `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` | Deterministic queue selection |\n| `promise.WriteOnce` | `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go` | Cross-goroutine dispatch signaling |\n| `eventclock.Interface` | `fairqueuing/eventclock/` | Mockable wall clock + deferred callbacks |\n| Work estimators | `flowcontrol/request/` | Seat count computation per request |\n| `metrics` package | `flowcontrol/metrics/` | Prometheus instrumentation |\n| `Integrator` | `fairqueuing/integrator.go` | Time-weighted seat-demand statistics |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `configController` \u2014 Configuration and Classification Layer\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`\n\nThe `configController` struct is the long-lived controller that:\n\n1. Watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API objects via informers and rebuilds the in-memory routing table whenever they change (`syncOne` \u2192 `digestConfigObjects` \u2192 `lockAndDigestConfigObjects`).\n2. Classifies every incoming request: iterates `cfgCtlr.flowSchemas` (sorted by ascending numerical `MatchingPrecedence`) and calls `matchesFlowSchema` until a match is found. The mandatory `catch-all` schema is always last, so no request goes unclassified (`startRequest`, line 1022).\n3. Derives the `flowDistinguisher` string from the matched FlowSchema's `DistinguisherMethod` (either the user name or the namespace), then computes a 64-bit hash via SHA-256 (`hashFlowID`, line 1131).\n4. Invokes `WorkEstimatorFunc` to get a `WorkEstimate` for the request (seats and optional additional latency).\n5. Delegates to `priorityLevelState.queues.StartRequest(...)` for admission and queuing.\n6. Runs a periodic borrowing rebalancer (`updateBorrowing`, every `borrowingAdjustmentPeriod` = 10 seconds) to dynamically redistribute unused concurrency across priority levels.\n\n**`priorityLevelState`** (line 202) ties together a `QueueSet`, the API object that configures it, the current concurrency limits (`nominalCL`, `minCL`, `maxCL`, `currentCL`), and a `seatDemandIntegrator` that accumulates demand statistics.\n\n### 2.2 `QueueSetFactory` / `QueueSetCompleter` \u2014 Two-Phase Construction\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/interface.go`, `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\nConstruction is split into two phases to allow configuration validation before committing to a concurrency slot:\n\n```\nQueueSetFactory.BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, ...) \u2192 QueueSetCompleter\nQueueSetCompleter.Complete(DispatchingConfig)         \u2192 QueueSet\n```\n\nThis matters because the `DispatchingConfig.ConcurrencyLimit` is computed by the borrowing algorithm after the `QueuingConfig` is already validated. The same two-phase pattern applies to reconfiguration (`QueueSet.BeginConfigChange`).\n\nOn `Complete`, the `queueSetCompleter` either constructs a new `queueSet` struct or reconfigures an existing one via `setConfiguration`, which:\n- Adds queues if `DesiredNumQueues` increased (existing queues drain via attrition, never forcibly removed).\n- Sets metric denominators.\n- Calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` immediately, so newly available capacity is used right away.\n\n### 2.3 `queueSet` \u2014 The Core Fair-Queuing Engine\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\n`queueSet` is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`. All methods that require the lock use the `Locked` suffix convention. The struct tracks:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `queues []*queue` | The array of per-flow virtual queues |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Global virtual-time progress meter R |\n| `lastRealTime time.Time` | Wall clock snapshot when R was last updated |\n| `robinIndex int` | Round-robin cursor for dispatch selection |\n| `totSeatsInUse int` | Current seat occupancy (used vs. `dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit`) |\n| `totRequestsWaiting int` | Count of queued-but-not-dispatched requests |\n| `dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer` | Queue selection engine |\n\n### 2.4 `queue` \u2014 Per-Flow Virtual Queue\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting   fifo               // FIFO list of waiting requests\n    nextDispatchR     SeatSeconds        // virtual clock: next dispatch time for this queue\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request] // currently executing requests\n    index             int                // position in queueSet.queues\n    seatsInUse        int                // seats occupied by executing requests\n}\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` is the core state for the WFQ algorithm: it advances by `totalWork` every time a request is dispatched from this queue, creating a virtual start time for the next request. This is what enforces per-queue fair share.\n\n### 2.5 `request` \u2014 Per-Request Tracking Object\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\nEach request carries:\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate` \u2014 initial seats \u00d7 estimated duration + final seats \u00d7 additional latency\n- `arrivalR SeatSeconds` \u2014 the value of `currentR` when the request arrived; used for the anti-windup bound\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 the dispatch/cancel decision, communicated from the dispatch goroutine to the waiting goroutine without the lock\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc` \u2014 O(1) removal from the FIFO list\n\n### 2.6 `fifo` / `requestFIFO` \u2014 Per-Queue FIFO List\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go`\n\nA standard `container/list.List` wrapper with an incrementally maintained `queueSum` (sum of `InitialSeats`, `MaxSeats`, and `totalWork` for all waiting requests). This allows O(1) aggregate queries used in both shuffle sharding and dispatch decisions.\n\n### 2.7 `promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 Dispatch Signaling\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\nA write-once, thread-safe value container. The `Get` method blocks until either:\n- `Set(decisionExecute)` is called (by the dispatcher, under the lock), or\n- The request's `context.Context` is cancelled (context deadline/cancellation propagates as `decisionCancel`).\n\nThis allows the waiting goroutine in `request.wait()` to block outside the lock while the dispatch goroutine operates under the lock.\n\n### 2.8 Work Estimators\n\n**Files:** `request/width.go`, `request/list_work_estimator.go`, `request/mutating_work_estimator.go`, `request/config.go`\n\nThe `WorkEstimator` maps HTTP verbs to seat estimates:\n\n- **Read-only non-list (get, watch without init events):** 1 seat (`MinimumSeats = 1`)\n- **List / watch with init events:** `ceil(estimatedObjects / objectsPerSeat)` seats (default: 1 seat per 100 objects), bounded by `MaximumListSeatsLimit` (default: 10, or 100 with `SizeBasedListCostEstimate` feature gate)\n- **Mutating (create/update/patch/delete):** 1 `InitialSeat` + optional `FinalSeats = ceil(watchCount / watchesPerSeat)` (default: 1 seat per 10 watches), with `AdditionalLatency` to model the cost of fan-out to watch handlers\n\nThe **two-phase seat model** is key: `InitialSeats` are held during the main body of request execution; `FinalSeats` (at a potentially different, usually smaller, count) are held for `AdditionalLatency` after the handler returns, representing the cost of dispatching change notifications to watch goroutines. This is deferred via `clock.EventAfterDuration` so it has no impact on client-observed latency.\n\n### 2.9 `shufflesharding.Dealer` \u2014 Queue Selection\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`\n\nThe `Dealer` implements a deterministic \"dealing a hand from a deck\" algorithm. Given a hash value and deck/hand sizes, it uses successive modulo extraction to produce a pseudo-random hand of `handSize` distinct queue indices from a deck of `deckSize` queues:\n\n```\nremainders[i] = hashValue mod (deckSize - i)\nhashValue     = hashValue / (deckSize - i)\n```\n\nThen a Fisher-Yates-like reconstruction maps remainders to actual indices. This uses `ceil(handSize \u00d7 log\u2082(deckSize))` bits of entropy, bounded by `MaxHashBits = 60`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Arrival: Classification and Hashing\n\n```\nHTTP request arrives at API server\n  \u2192 apf_filter.go: configController.Handle(ctx, requestDigest, ...)\n    \u2192 configController.startRequest(ctx, rd, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn)\n      \u2192 iterate cfgCtlr.flowSchemas (sorted by MatchingPrecedence)\n        \u2192 rule.go: matchesFlowSchema(rd, fs)  [subject + resource/nonResource rules]\n      \u2192 computeFlowDistinguisher(rd, fs.Spec.DistinguisherMethod)\n        \u2192 user name OR namespace\n      \u2192 hashFlowID(fsName, flowDistinguisher)  [SHA-256 \u2192 uint64]\n      \u2192 workEstimator()  [called here, result passed to StartRequest]\n      \u2192 plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n```\n\nThe `flowDistinguisher` determines which \"flow\" this request belongs to. Two requests from the same user (distinguisher = user name) or in the same namespace (distinguisher = namespace) map to the same flow, and thus are likely to land in the same queue via shuffle sharding\u2014enabling per-flow isolation.\n\n### 3.2 Queue Assignment: Shuffle Sharding\n\nInside `StartRequest` (`queueset.go:308`), if `DesiredNumQueues >= 1`, the request goes through `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`:\n\n```\nshuffleShardLocked(hashValue, ...)\n  \u2192 dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])   // deals handSize queue indices\n  \u2192 offset = qs.enqueues % handSize               // staggered starting position (anti-bias)\n  \u2192 for each queue in hand:\n      thisQueueSeatSeconds = queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n      track minimum\n  \u2192 return bestQueueIdx  (minimum total waiting work)\n```\n\nThe shuffle-sharding property: with `handSize = 8` out of `deckSize = 128` queues, the probability that two distinct flows share all 8 queues is `(8/128)^8 \u2248 10^{-10}`. Even a noisy neighbor running thousands of requests can only fill 8 queues; the other flow's 8 queues will almost certainly include some with lower occupancy, limiting blast radius.\n\nThe **minimum-work selection** (not minimum-length) within the dealt hand means a queue with few but large requests is still preferred over a queue with many small ones\u2014proportional to actual resource cost.\n\n### 3.3 Reject or Enqueue\n\n`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` (`queueset.go:618`) enforces:\n\n```\nif totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit:\n    return false  // reject: full queue + full concurrency\n```\n\nNote the **AND** condition: a queue that is full can still accept requests if there is remaining concurrency. Only when *both* limits are hit is the request rejected with a `queue-full` metric tag.\n\n`enqueueToBoundLocked` (`queueset.go:632`) adds the request to the FIFO list, initializes `queue.nextDispatchR = currentR` if the queue was empty (so a fresh queue doesn't inherit a stale virtual start time), and updates all counters and metrics atomically.\n\n### 3.4 Dispatch: Virtual Time and Round-Robin Selection\n\nAfter enqueue, `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs a loop:\n\n```\nwhile totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit:\n    dispatchLocked()\n```\n\n`dispatchLocked` calls `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` which scans all queues in **round-robin order** (advancing `robinIndex` by 1 each iteration) and selects the queue whose head request has the **minimum virtual finish time**:\n\n```\nvirtualFinish(queue) = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\nThis is the FIFO WFQ criterion: the queue that would finish soonest in the virtual world goes next. Among ties, the round-robin ordering provides an implicit secondary sort.\n\n**Concurrency check before dispatch:**\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) canAccommodateSeatsLocked(seats int) bool {\n    if seats > ConcurrencyLimit && totRequestsExecuting == 0:\n        return true   // oversized request: allow only when server is empty\n    return totSeatsInUse + seats <= ConcurrencyLimit\n}\n```\n\nIf the head of the selected queue cannot be accommodated, `dispatchLocked` returns `false` and the loop stops. No other queue is tried \u2014 the system waits for running requests to complete and free seats.\n\n**Post-dispatch accounting** (`queueset.go:741`):\n\n```go\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n```\n\nThis is the heart of the WFQ algorithm: after dispatching, the queue's virtual clock advances by the request's work, making it \"more expensive\" relative to other queues and ensuring it will not be selected again until the others catch up.\n\n### 3.5 Waiting: The `promise.WriteOnce` Pattern\n\nThe client goroutine (the HTTP handler goroutine) returns from `StartRequest` with a non-nil `fq.Request` and calls `req.Finish(execFn)`. Internally this calls `req.wait()` which blocks on `req.decision.Get()`. This call releases the per-goroutine stack into a channel select:\n\n```go\nfunc (p *promise) Get() interface{} {\n    select {\n    case <-p.setCh:           // dispatch goroutine called Set(decisionExecute)\n    case <-p.doneCtx.Done(): // request context cancelled (timeout)\n        p.Set(p.doneVal)      // doneVal = decisionCancel\n    }\n    return p.value\n}\n```\n\nThis design ensures the waiting goroutine never holds the `queueSet.lock` while blocking. When the request's context expires, `decisionCancel` is set and `request.wait()` removes the request from its queue, decrements counters, and records a `time-out` metric (`queueset.go:427\u2013438`).\n\n### 3.6 Execution and Completion\n\nOn `decisionExecute`, `Finish` calls `execFn()` \u2014 the real HTTP handler. On return, `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible` is called:\n\n1. **`finishRequestLocked`** (`queueset.go:863`):\n   - Decrements `totRequestsExecuting`.\n   - Removes request from `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n   - **Adjusts `queue.nextDispatchR`** for actual vs. estimated service time:\n     ```go\n     queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(float64(r.InitialSeats()), estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n     ```\n     If the request ran *faster* than `estimatedServiceDuration` (default: 3ms), `nextDispatchR` is *moved earlier*, crediting the queue; if slower, it moves later \u2014 a soft real-time feedback loop.\n   - If `AdditionalLatency > 0`, defers `releaseSeatsLocked` via `clock.EventAfterDuration`, then calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` again from the deferred callback.\n\n2. **`removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`**: If the queue is now empty and the total queue count exceeds `DesiredNumQueues`, the queue is removed and `robinIndex` is adjusted.\n\n3. **`boundNextDispatchLocked`** (anti-windup): Ensures `queue.nextDispatchR` never falls below the `arrivalR` of the oldest waiting request. Without this, a queue that received small requests and finished them quickly would accumulate a very early `nextDispatchR`, creating an unfair advantage.\n\n### 3.7 Virtual Time Synchronization\n\n`syncTimeLocked` is called every time the lock is acquired (`lockAndSyncTime`). It advances `currentR` based on elapsed real time and the current virtual time ratio:\n\n```go\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\n`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked` computes:\n\n```go\nratio = min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nwhere `seatsRequested` is the sum over all queues of `(seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum of waiting requests)`. This ratio equals the number of seat-seconds allocated per queue per second. When no queues are active, the ratio is zero and `currentR` freezes.\n\n**Epoch management** (`advanceEpoch`): When `currentR` approaches `MaxSeatSeconds/2`, all queue `nextDispatchR` values and request `arrivalR` values are decremented by `MaxSeatSeconds/2` to prevent overflow. This is an O(N) operation proportional to the number of queues and waiting requests.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Borrowing Algorithm: Dynamic Concurrency Reallocation\n\nThe `configController` runs `updateBorrowing` every 10 seconds to redistibute unused concurrency across priority levels. This is layered above the per-`QueueSet` dispatch and uses seat demand statistics tracked by the `Integrator`.\n\n**Seat demand stats** (`priorityLevelState.seatDemandStats`):\n- The `Integrator` (`fairqueuing/integrator.go`) tracks the time-integral of `totSeatsInUse + totSeatsWaiting` as a continuous function, computing mean, standard deviation, and high watermark over each adjustment period.\n- `envelope = avg + stdDev` estimates a \"typical peak\".\n- `smoothed = max(envelope, A*smoothed + (1-A)*envelope)` with decay coefficient `A = 0.977` (half-life \u2248 5 minutes) prevents oscillation.\n\n**`computeConcurrencyAllocation`** (`conc_alloc.go:119`) solves a bounded proportional allocation problem:\n\n- **Inputs:** each priority level's `target = max(minCurrentCL, smoothed demand)`, `lowerBound = minCL`, `upperBound = maxCL`.\n- **Constraint:** sum of allocations = `nominalCLSum`.\n- **Algorithm:** find a single scalar `fairProp` such that `alloc[i] = clamp(fairProp \u00d7 target[i], lower[i], upper[i])` and the allocations sum correctly. This is solved by sorting the bounds and scanning linearly \u2014 O(N log N) per adjustment cycle.\n\nEach priority level's `currentCL` is set to the allocation result, and `plState.qsCompleter.Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL, ...})` is called, which calls `setConfiguration` on the `queueSet`, immediately triggering `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`.\n\n**Config limits that feed borrowing:**\n- `NominalConcurrencyShares`: proportional weight in the initial allocation.\n- `LendablePercent`: what fraction of nominal can be lent to others. `minCL = nominalCL \u00d7 (1 - lendablePercent/100)`.\n- `BorrowingLimitPercent`: how much above nominal can be borrowed. `maxCL = nominalCL \u00d7 (1 + borrowingLimitPercent/100)`.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Rejection Under Load\n\nThere are two rejection paths:\n\n1. **No-queue mode** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`): immediate reject if `totSeatsInUse + MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`. Used for priority levels configured with `LimitResponse.Type: Reject`.\n2. **Queue-full**: rejected if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`. The AND condition means a full queue is *not* sufficient alone \u2014 there must also be no available concurrency. This is intentional: it avoids rejecting requests that could be dispatched immediately if concurrency were available.\n\nRejected requests get metric tag `\"queue-full\"` or `\"concurrency-limit\"` via `metrics.AddReject`.\n\n### 5.2 Context Cancellation / Timeout\n\nWhen a request's context is cancelled while waiting, `promise.Get` unblocks via `<-p.doneCtx.Done()` and `decisionCancel` is set. The `wait()` method then calls `removeFromQueueLocked()` to atomically remove the request and update all counters, including `boundNextDispatchLocked` to re-check the anti-windup bound on the now-modified queue head.\n\nThe double-decrement protection (checking `e.Value == nil` in the `removeFromFIFOFunc` closure) ensures idempotent removal even if the request was concurrently dispatched.\n\n### 5.3 Oversized Requests (seats > ConcurrencyLimit)\n\n`canAccommodateSeatsLocked` (`queueset.go:748`) has a special case: if a single request's `MaxSeats` exceeds `ConcurrencyLimit`, it is allowed to execute only when the server is completely idle (`totRequestsExecuting == 0`). This prevents starvation of such requests but causes them to block all other dispatches until they complete. A log warning is emitted if `totalWork > rDecrement/100`.\n\nAdditionally, at dispatch time, if `FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`, `FinalSeats` is clamped to `ConcurrencyLimit` and `AdditionalLatency` is scaled up proportionally to preserve total work:\n\n```go\nadditionalLatency = finalWork.DurationPerSeat(float64(finalSeats))\n```\n\n### 5.4 Tradeoffs in the Virtual Time Model\n\n**All non-empty queues advance at the same rate.** `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked` divides available capacity equally among active queues, regardless of their actual seat demand. A queue with one thin request and a queue with ten fat requests both get the same virtual time increment. This is correct for isolation (each active flow gets a fair share), but can cause suboptimal dispatch ordering when seat demands are heterogeneous.\n\n**Estimated service duration is fixed** at `3 * time.Millisecond` (set in `Complete`). This constant interacts with `nextDispatchR` adjustment: if actual service is systematically much shorter or longer, the anti-windup bounds may be loose. There is no feedback from real latency into the estimate itself.\n\n**The round-robin tie-breaking** in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` means that if all queues have the same `virtualFinish`, the queue just after the last dispatched queue wins. This provides a weak fairness guarantee when work estimates are equal but does not track actual byte throughput.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 6.1 `promiseFactoryFactory` \u2014 Testability Hook\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\nInjected via `newTestableQueueSetFactory`. In production this always returns `promise.NewWriteOnce`. Tests substitute a factory that records or controls dispatch signals. Misuse in production (e.g., a blocking factory) would deadlock the dispatch goroutine.\n\n### 6.2 `eventclock.Interface` \u2014 Clock Abstraction\n\n`queueSet.clock` is an `eventclock.Interface`, not the standard `time.Now`. This allows tests to advance virtual time and trigger `EventAfterDuration` callbacks without sleeping. Replacing this in production with a slow or faulty clock would corrupt all virtual time calculations.\n\n### 6.3 `WorkEstimatorFunc` \u2014 Pluggable Cost Model\n\n`NewWorkEstimator` in `request/width.go` is called from the APF filter and returns a `WorkEstimatorFunc`. It is structured as a composable function (not an interface), making it easy to replace the entire cost function or wrap it with a decorator. The cost model directly affects both scheduling fairness and the anti-starvation behavior for wide requests.\n\n**Risks:**\n- Underestimating list cost (e.g., for aggregated APIs where `ObjectCountNotFoundErr` returns `minSeats = 1`) means such requests occupy fewer virtual queue slots, potentially giving them an unfair advantage.\n- Overestimating watch fan-out cost blocks dispatching other requests while the queue accumulates enough seats to accommodate the wide request.\n\n### 6.4 `QueueSetFactory` Interface \u2014 Queuing Backend Replacement\n\nThe `configController` depends only on the `fq.QueueSetFactory` interface (`fairqueuing/interface.go`), injected at construction. An alternative fair-queuing backend (e.g., one with per-priority weighted scheduling or a deficit round-robin variant) could be injected without changing the controller logic. The interface contract is minimal: `BeginConstruction`, `Complete`, `StartRequest`, `Finish`, `IsIdle`, `Dump`.\n\n### 6.5 `MaxSeatsTracker` \u2014 Per-Priority-Level Seat Caps\n\n`MaxSeatsTracker` (`apf_controller.go:157`) tracks per-priority-level max seats used by the work estimator. It is set in `finishQueueSetReconfigsLocked` (`line 892`):\n\n```go\nmaxSeats = MAX(1, MIN(0.15 \u00d7 nominalCL, nominalCL / handSize))\n```\n\nThis ensures the max seats cap scales with the priority level's concurrency allocation, preventing a single list request from consuming more than 15% of a level's concurrency. Changing `priorityLevelMaxSeatsPercent` from its current `0.15` would shift the balance between large-request throughput and multi-tenant fairness.\n\n### 6.6 FlowSchema and Priority Level Config \u2014 Operator Customization\n\nOperators customize APF behavior exclusively through Kubernetes API objects:\n- `FlowSchema.Spec.Rules` \u2014 what requests match, with what distinguisher\n- `PriorityLevelConfiguration.Spec.Limited.LimitResponse.Queuing` \u2014 `Queues`, `QueueLengthLimit`, `HandSize`\n- `NominalConcurrencyShares`, `LendablePercent`, `BorrowingLimitPercent`\n\n**Risk:** Setting `HandSize` close to `Queues` (e.g., `HandSize = Queues`) eliminates the shuffle-sharding isolation benefit: every flow sees all queues, and a noisy neighbor can fill them all. Setting `HandSize = 1` is pure hashing (no election among candidates), breaking the \"choose best of hand\" anti-noisy-neighbor property. The sweet spot for defaults (e.g., `HandSize = 8, Queues = 128`) provides `(8/128)^8 \u2248 10^{-10}` collision probability.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance\n\n**Lock contention:** All QueueSet state is guarded by a single `sync.Mutex`. Under high request rates, this mutex is acquired and released for every `StartRequest`, every dispatch cycle, and every `finishRequestLocked`. The lock is held briefly (no I/O, no slow computation inside), but at very high concurrency (thousands of RPS per priority level) contention may become visible. The `configController`'s `lock.RLock()` during `startRequest` is separate and allows concurrent classification reads.\n\n**`syncTimeLocked` on every lock acquisition:** Every call to `lockAndSyncTime` advances virtual time. This is O(1) arithmetic. However, if `advanceEpoch` is triggered (every ~2^63 seat-nanoseconds of accumulated work at scale), it is O(queues \u00d7 waitingRequests). This should be extremely rare in practice.\n\n**`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` loop:** In the worst case (many queues, many requests), each `dispatchLocked` call scans all queues via round-robin. O(numQueues) per dispatch. With `Queues = 128` and `ConcurrencyLimit = 400`, the loop runs at most 400 times per invocation, touching 128 queues each time: 51,200 iterations per fully-loaded dispatch cycle. This is bounded and predictable.\n\n### 7.2 Reliability\n\n**Mandatory FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations:** `imaginePL` (`apf_controller.go:991`) synthesizes the mandatory `exempt` and `catch-all` objects if they are absent from the API, ensuring the system is never stuck with an unclassified request. Deleting these objects is recoverable because the controller will re-create them (in memory) on the next sync.\n\n**Quiescing priority levels:** When a PLC is deleted, its `priorityLevelState.quiescing` is set to true. The QueueSet continues to drain. Only after `queues.IsIdle()` is confirmed does the controller trigger a config reload that removes the state. This prevents requests already queued against a deleted level from being abruptly cancelled.\n\n**Double-dispatch prevention:** `promise.WriteOnce` uses `sync.Once` to ensure `Set` is idempotent. If a request's context fires and `decisionCancel` is set while `dispatchLocked` simultaneously calls `Set(decisionExecute)`, only the first write wins. The dispatch loop detects the lost race via `!request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)` and continues without changing seat counts (the request is no longer in the queue but never entered `executing` state).\n\n**FlowSchema status update rate limiting:** `shouldDelayUpdate` tracks how often each FlowSchema has had its status updated. If the same schema is updated more than 5 times in a minute, subsequent updates are delayed by a random 30\u201375 second jitter to prevent thundering-herd status updates when many apiservers are reconciling simultaneously.\n\n### 7.3 Maintainability\n\n**The `Locked` naming convention** is strictly enforced in the queueset package: every method that requires `qs.lock` held has the `Locked` suffix, and `ToBoundLocked` signals that `boundNextDispatchLocked` must be called afterward. Violating this convention would introduce subtle data races.\n\n**Metrics integration is pervasive.** Every state transition (enqueue, dispatch, reject, finish, seat change) updates Prometheus gauges and counters. The `seatDemandIntegrator` provides continuous time-weighted statistics for the borrowing algorithm. Missing a metric update in a new code path would silently corrupt the borrowing decisions.\n\n**The config digest is all-or-nothing:** `lockAndDigestConfigObjects` reads all FlowSchemas and PLCs at once and atomically replaces `cfgCtlr.flowSchemas` and `cfgCtlr.priorityLevelStates`. Partial updates are not possible. This simplifies reasoning but means any validation error for one object (e.g., a bad HandSize) causes that object to be dropped from the active config entirely, not just flagged.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go` | HTTP handler entry point: `Interface`, `New`, `Handle` |\n| # Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### Purpose

The API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem implements fair multi-tenant queuing for the Kubernetes API server. Its core responsibility is to ensure that no single client or workload monopolizes API server capacity—even under heavy load—while still providing guaranteed minimum throughput and bounded latency to every priority class.

The subsystem is the realization of the "Fair Queuing for Server Requests" algorithm described in [KEP-1040](https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md). It adapts the classic WFQ (Weighted Fair Queuing) technique to a stateless, per-request server context, replacing per-byte cost accounting with per-seat-second cost accounting.

### Subsystem Boundaries

**Upstream (what feeds the QueueSet):**

- The `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) classifies each incoming request against an ordered list of `FlowSchema` objects, selects a matching `PriorityLevelConfiguration`, computes a flow distinguisher hash, estimates work, and calls `QueueSet.StartRequest`.
- The HTTP filter entry point is `configController.Handle` (`apf_filter.go:155`), which is invoked by the API server's handler chain for every non-exempt request.

**Downstream (what the QueueSet controls):**

- The `execFn` callback passed to `Handle` — the actual request handler. The QueueSet decides whether to call it, delay it (queued wait), or suppress it (reject).

**Peer dependencies:**

| Component | Location | Role |
|-----------|----------|------|
| `shufflesharding.Dealer` | `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` | Deterministic queue selection |

... (truncated)
